## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor rate laws / ODE kinetics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard form of a kinetic rate law in homogeneous reaction kinetics. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where reaction order (in A) and/or time-varying effective rate constants (e.g., catalyst decay, forcing) determine dA_dt.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or saturated kinetics over the observed range)
- First-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition, dilute-limit kinetics)
- Second-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or A + A -> products)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general empirical reaction order fitting)
- Reversible/relaxation-to-equilibrium form: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1 with rate constant c0)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type in A) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth/decay with limiting concentration)
- Parallel decay channels (sum of orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order pathways)
- Time-dependent first-order (catalyst deactivation/aging): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decreases exponentially in time)
- Time-dependent first-order (activation/warm-up): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps up from 0 to c0 due to mixing/heating/activation)
- Induction-time shifted kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(-c1 * (t - c2))) (delayed onset followed by near-first-order decay)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood-type inhibition/surface coverage: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate suppressed at high A due to site saturation/adsorption competition)
- Stronger adsorption limitation: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (rate decreases more steeply with A when both reactant and inhibitor occupy sites)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Order identification: if dA_dt vs A is linear through the origin, first-order (-c*A) is likely; curvature consistent with A**2 suggests second-order; log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) slope indicates reaction order.
- Equilibrium/reversibility signature: if dA_dt changes sign at a finite A (crosses zero near A ≈ c1), a relaxation term c*(c1 - A) or reversible net rate is plausible.
- Autocatalysis signature: if |dA_dt| is small at low A, increases at intermediate A, then decreases near an upper bound, terms like A*(c1 - A) are suggested.
- Multiple pathways: if a single power law cannot fit both low-A and high-A regimes, additive terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) often capture parallel mechanisms.
- Catalyst deactivation/aging: if the apparent rate constant decreases over time at similar A, include multiplicative time factors like exp(-c*t) or (1 + c*t)**(-p).
- Induction/mixing delay: if reaction is initially slow and then accelerates without requiring high A, incorporate time-gating factors like (1 - exp(-c*(t-c0))).
- Surface/adsorption limitation: if rate increases with A at low A but levels off or is suppressed at high A, rational forms with (1 + c*A)^n in the denominator are common in heterogeneous/adsorption-influenced kinetics.
- External forcing/feed effects: if dA_dt shows periodic or non-monotone time dependence not explainable by A alone, add explicit t-driving terms (e.g., +c*sin(c*t) or +c*exp(-c*t)) to represent illumination, pulsing, or intermittent dosing.

If set \(c1=0\) to remove it, you lose \(A^{1/3}\). **No match**.
